185, 611, 2024-12-16 00:00:00, 22, confirmed unit names with site
184, 576, 2024-12-04 00:00:00, 22, PRESS RELEASE
EP NL CLOSES RIJNMOND 1 POWER PLANT DUE TO
UNPREDICTABLE MARKET CONDITIONS
2.12.2024
Middelburg, 2.12.2024 - EP NL, one of the largest electricity producers in the Netherlands, took an
important step today. The company strongly considers the decommissioning of one of its gas-fired
power plants, Rijnmond 1, located in the port of Rotterdam, from 2nd quarter 2026.
Uncertain market conditions
The development of renewable energy, such as wind and solar power, is at no doubt a key step
in reducing CO₂ emissions. However, their natural intermittency makes balancing the grid more
and more challenging. In the Dutch and broader European electricity market, gas fired power
plants still play a crucial role in ensuring security of supply and system reliability.
However, the power market hardly provides adequate revenue streams or sufficient predictability
to sustain their future operations. Further investments and operations are not economically viable
under current market conditions and design. EP NL therefore has started the plan to
decommission the Rijnmond 1 power plant as of 31 March 2026.
At the same time, EP NL is willing to invest in new, flexible solutions that contribute to a sustainable
and balanced energy market and has started to develop alternatives for its power plant.
Quote “This decision aims at sending a clear signal to the Dutch market about the necessity of a
capacity market or an equivalent mechanism. We call upon all relevant stakeholders to address the
serious issue of a sustained reliability of the Dutch electricity supply, for which we remain firmly
committed.” says Peter Černák, Chairman of the Board of EP NL.
About EP NL
EP NL is a major player in the Dutch energy market. We focus on power generation, trading and
energy solutions for businesses. Our efficient and flexible power plants ensure a stable and
controllable supply of electricity in the Netherlands. We integrate renewable energy sources and
provide the necessary flexibility to the electricity market. EP NL is committed to a reliable,
sustainable energy future and an efficient energy supply for the Netherlands. We actively shape
the energy landscape by providing efficient solutions for today and investing in innovative
technologies for the future.
Rijnmond 1
Rijnmond 1 is a gas-fired power plant located on the Vondelingenplaat near Rotterdam Pernis. De
total capacity of the power plan is 750 MW.
Media
For more information or inquiries please contact: press@epnl.nl. Please send your request and/or
question by email, and we will get back to you as soon as possible.
For more information about our company please visit epnl.nl.

1400, 2188, 2024-11-01 00:00:00, 22, Hi Mark, 

I wanted to circle back on this. We’ve reached out to some of our other industry contacts (and had people ask around at AFPM) to get a better understanding of how we might be seeing arsenic in the SCR catalyst. 

Like you said, it had to be going through the burner. Based on the feedback we have received, our current understanding here at Lemont is that Canadian syn crudes have a significantly higher concentration of arsenic than other crudes. We’ve been running an increased amount of syn crude over the last few years. In the FCC, arsine (AsH3) is produced and has a boiling point between ethane and ethylene, so it can get into our fuel gas system. From there it will make its way to the boilers. 

I’ll be interested to hear if you find increased arsenic poisoning going forward with sites that are running syn crude (and not treating their fuel gas system for arsenic) like we are. 

Hope you find this information helpful or at least interesting. 

Best, 

Matt Budde
1401, 2187, 2024-11-01 00:00:00, 22, Hi Mark, 

I wanted to circle back on this. We’ve reached out to some of our other industry contacts (and had people ask around at AFPM) to get a better understanding of how we might be seeing arsenic in the SCR catalyst. 

Like you said, it had to be going through the burner. Based on the feedback we have received, our current understanding here at Lemont is that Canadian syn crudes have a significantly higher concentration of arsenic than other crudes. We’ve been running an increased amount of syn crude over the last few years. In the FCC, arsine (AsH3) is produced and has a boiling point between ethane and ethylene, so it can get into our fuel gas system. From there it will make its way to the boilers. 

I’ll be interested to hear if you find increased arsenic poisoning going forward with sites that are running syn crude (and not treating their fuel gas system for arsenic) like we are. 

Hope you find this information helpful or at least interesting. 

Best, 

Matt Budde
